\doxysubsection{Detailed Description}
\subsubsection*{template$<$size\+\_\+t Max\+Static\+Size = 0, class Allocator = std\+::allocator$<$char$>$$>$\newline
class seq\+::tiny\+\_\+string$<$ Max\+Static\+Size, Allocator $>$}

String class with a similar interface and requirements than std\+::string. 


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em Max\+Static\+Size} & maximum static size for Small String Optimization \\
\hline
{\em Allocator} & allocator type\\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}
\mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string}{seq\+::tiny\+\_\+string}} is a string class similar to std\+::string but aiming at greater performances when used in containers. It provides a customizable Small String Optimization (S\+SO) much like boost\+::small\+\_\+vector, where the maximum static size before an allocation is triggered is defined at compile time.

\mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string}{seq\+::tiny\+\_\+string}} contains some preallocated elements in-\/place, which can avoid the use of dynamic storage allocation when the actual number of elements is below that preallocated threshold (Max\+Static\+Size parameter).

\mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string}{seq\+::tiny\+\_\+string}} only supports characters of type char, not wchar\+\_\+t.\hypertarget{classseq_1_1tiny__string_autotoc_md53}{}\doxysubsubsection{Size and bookkeeping}\label{classseq_1_1tiny__string_autotoc_md53}
By default, a \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string}{tiny\+\_\+string}} contains enough room to store a 15 bytes string, therefore a length of 14 bytes for null terminated strings. For small strings (below the preallocated threshold), \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string}{tiny\+\_\+string}} only store one additional byte for bookkeeping\+: 7 bits for string length and 1 bit to tell if the string is allocated in-\/place or on the heap. It means that the default \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string}{tiny\+\_\+string}} size is 16 bytes, which is half the size of std\+::string on gcc and msvc. This small footprint is what makes \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string}{tiny\+\_\+string}} very fast on flat containers like std\+::vector ot std\+::deque, while node based container (like std\+::map) are less impacted. Note that this tiny size is only reach when using std\+::allocator$<$char$>$.

When the \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string}{tiny\+\_\+string}} grows beyong the preallocated threshold, memory is allocated on the heap based on provided allocator, and the bookkeeping part is divided as follow\+:
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item still 1 bit to tell is the memory is heap allocated or not,
\item 1 bit to tell if the string capacity is exactly equal to the string size + 1 (as \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string}{tiny\+\_\+string}} is always null terminated),
\item sizeof(size\+\_\+t)$\ast$8 -\/ 2 bits to store the string size. Therefore, the maximum size of \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string}{tiny\+\_\+string}} is slightly lower than std\+::string.
\item a pointer (4 to 8 bytes) to the actual memory chunk.
\end{DoxyItemize}

\mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string}{seq\+::tiny\+\_\+string}} does not store the memory capacity, and always use a grow factor of 2. The capacity is always deduced from the string length using compiler intrinsics (like \+\_\+\+Bit\+Scan\+Reverse on msvc). In some cases (like copy construction), the allocated capacity is the same as the string length, in which case a 1 bit flag is set to track this information.

The global typedef \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceseq_a8d9a01a2c5a12df6d4baac1d1520d4b5}{seq\+::tstring}} is provided for convenience, and is equivalent to \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string}{seq\+::tiny\+\_\+string}}$<$0,std\+::allocator$<$char$>$$>$.\hypertarget{classseq_1_1tiny__string_autotoc_md54}{}\doxysubsubsection{Static size}\label{classseq_1_1tiny__string_autotoc_md54}
The maximum preallocated space is specified as a template parameter (Max\+Static\+Size). By default, this value is set to 0, meaning that the \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string}{tiny\+\_\+string}} only uses 2 word of either 32 or 64 bits depending on the architecture. Therefore, the maximum in-\/place capacity is either 7 or 15 bytes.

The maximum preallocated space can be increased up to 126 bytes. To have a \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string}{tiny\+\_\+string}} of 32 bytes like std\+::string on gcc and msvc, you could use, for instance, tiny\+\_\+string$<$28$>$. In this case, the maximum string size (excluding null-\/terminated character) to use S\+SO would be 30 bytes (!).

For std\+::allocator$<$char$>$, the allocator object is not stored inside the \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string}{tiny\+\_\+string}}, ensuring a minimal space overhead. If a custom allocator is provided, it will be stored as part of the string object and used for heap allocations/deallocations.\hypertarget{classseq_1_1tiny__string_autotoc_md55}{}\doxysubsubsection{Relocatable type}\label{classseq_1_1tiny__string_autotoc_md55}
\mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string}{seq\+::tiny\+\_\+string}} is relocatable, meaning that it does not store pointer to internal data. Relocatable types can be used more efficiently in containers that are aware of this property. For instance, \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1devector}{seq\+::devector}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1deque}{seq\+::deque}} and \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1flat__map}{seq\+::flat\+\_\+map}} are faster when working with relocatable types, as the process to move one object from a memory layout about to be destroyed to a new one can be accomplished through a simple memcpy.

Msvc implementation of std\+::string is also relocatable, while gcc implementation is not as it stores a pointer to its internal data for small string.

Within the seq library, a relocatable type must statify \mbox{\hyperlink{structseq_1_1is__relocatable_a9bc3104d310961a601c2185957f846ad}{seq\+::is\+\_\+relocatable$<$type$>$\+::value}} == true.\hypertarget{classseq_1_1tiny__string_autotoc_md56}{}\doxysubsubsection{Interface}\label{classseq_1_1tiny__string_autotoc_md56}
\mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string}{seq\+::tiny\+\_\+string}} provides the same interface as std\+::string. Functions working on other strings like \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string_ae21be406c9d1e1bc48e4bfce9643a3b2}{find()}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string_afd17882c7d4d62dd19d972f2caefeb9c}{compare()}}... are overloaded to also work on std\+::string. The comparison operators are also overloaded to work with std\+::string.

\mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string}{seq\+::tiny\+\_\+string}} provides the following additional members for convenience\+:
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string_a321d02c7a86f9394fcb039783f38f49d}{join()}}\+: merge several strings with a common separator
\item \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string_a8879c2a3587a80a7cceb17ad60d66b35}{split()}}\+: split string based on separator
\item \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string_aedb0a92e0d788252ee5a7ed486b88db4}{replace()}}\+: replace a string by another one
\item \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string_a3399642306574c8ac4929bd0e638adce}{convert()}}\+: convert the string to another type using streams
\item \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string_abe4bcb33df9d4dcc21c6b87cc47a49b4}{sprintf()}}\+: format string
\end{DoxyItemize}

\mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string}{seq\+::tiny\+\_\+string}} also works with std\+::istream/std\+::ostream exactly like std\+::string. A specialization of std\+::hash is provided for \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string}{tiny\+\_\+string}} types which relies on murmurhash2. This specialization is transparent and supports hashing std\+::string, \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string}{tiny\+\_\+string}} and const char$\ast$.

\mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string}{seq\+::tiny\+\_\+string}} provides the same invalidation rules as std\+::string as well as the same exception guarantees.

The main difference compared to std\+::string is memory deallocation. As \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string}{tiny\+\_\+string}} does not store the capacity internally, its capacity is deduced from the size and must be the closest greater or equal power of 2 (except for a few situations where the capacity is excatly the length +1). Therefore, \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string}{tiny\+\_\+string}} must release memory when its size decreases due, for instance, to calls to \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string_a91ae02f14ccf8872ff5a584247af3742}{tiny\+\_\+string\+::pop\+\_\+back()}}. Likewise, \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string_a3c3ef3a777285f5d9e11e15ce32c50de}{shrink\+\_\+to\+\_\+fit()}} and \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string_ab339c6b163b605508b67e8c354b5f181}{reserve()}} are no-\/ops.\hypertarget{classseq_1_1tiny__string_autotoc_md57}{}\doxysubsubsection{String view}\label{classseq_1_1tiny__string_autotoc_md57}
\mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string}{seq\+::tiny\+\_\+string}} is specialized for \mbox{\hyperlink{structseq_1_1view__allocator}{seq\+::view\+\_\+allocator}} in order to provide a std\+::string\+\_\+view like class. It is provided for compilers that do not support (yet) std\+::string\+\_\+view, and provides a similar interface.

The global typedef \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceseq_a2bede5ff16f5bb9f856b3b2d78303f69}{seq\+::tstring\+\_\+view}} is provided for convenience, and is equivalent to seq\+::tiny\+\_\+string$<$0,seq\+::view\+\_\+allocator$>$. tstring\+\_\+view is also hashable and can be compared to other \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string}{tiny\+\_\+string}} types as well as std\+::string.\hypertarget{classseq_1_1tiny__string_autotoc_md58}{}\doxysubsubsection{Performances}\label{classseq_1_1tiny__string_autotoc_md58}
All \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string}{tiny\+\_\+string}} members have been optimized to match or outperform most std\+::string implementations. They have been benchmarked against gcc (10.\+0.\+1) and msvc (14.\+20) for members \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string_afd17882c7d4d62dd19d972f2caefeb9c}{compare()}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string_ae21be406c9d1e1bc48e4bfce9643a3b2}{find()}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string_abb8cedeada19a42176d5caecbffefab5}{rfind()}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string_a6b21adbddd6cccd2141fb87fba9b7b60}{find\+\_\+first\+\_\+of()}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string_a6dbd8181ad25d9672f76840b13bd9802}{find\+\_\+last\+\_\+of()}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string_a17b27090ca94b3d4747725e8b43c8c47}{find\+\_\+first\+\_\+not\+\_\+of()}} and \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string_a7853b24ec695748a54a5222fe143c611}{find\+\_\+last\+\_\+not\+\_\+of()}}.

Appending back characters is also slightly faster, as well as comparison operators. The only exception is the \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string_a91ae02f14ccf8872ff5a584247af3742}{pop\+\_\+back()}} member that can be slower than msvc and gcc implementations.

\mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string}{tiny\+\_\+string}} is usually faster when used inside flat containers simply because its size is smaller than std\+::string (32 bytes on gcc and msvc). The following table shows the performances of \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string}{tiny\+\_\+string}} against std\+::string for sorting a vector of 1M random short string (size = 14, where both \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string}{tiny\+\_\+string}} and std\+::string use S\+SO) and 1M random longer strings (size = 200, both use heap allocation). Tested with gcc 10.\+1.\+0 (-\/O3) for msys2 on Windows 10, using Intel(\+R) Core(\+T\+M) i7-\/10850H at 2.\+70\+G\+Hz.

\tabulinesep=1mm
\begin{longtabu}spread 0pt [c]{*{5}{|X[-1]}|}

\endfirsthead

\endfoot

\end{longtabu}


Note that \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string}{tiny\+\_\+string}} always uses its own comparison function. We can see that the comparison function of \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string}{tiny\+\_\+string}} is faster than the default one used by std\+::string. Even when using \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string}{tiny\+\_\+string}} comparator, std\+::string remains slightly slower due to the tinier memory footprint of \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string}{tiny\+\_\+string}}.

The difference is wider on msvc (14.\+20)\+:

{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$size\+\_\+t Max\+Static\+Size = 0, class Allocator  = std\+::allocator$<$char$>$$>$ \\
void \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string}{seq\+::tiny\+\_\+string}}$<$ Max\+Static\+Size, Allocator $>$\+::resize (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{size\+\_\+t}]{n,  }\item[{char}]{c }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}



Resize the string. For wide string, the allocated memory will be of exactly n+1 bytes. If n is bigger than \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiny__string_a459229f255e73ebba8c822d3d78b9799}{size()}}, pad with (n-\/size()) copies of c.

Split the string based on the substring match. Computed strings are stored in output itreator out. If keep\+\_\+empty\+\_\+strings is false, empty strings are not added to the output iterator. 

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
New past-\/the-\/end output iterator 
\end{DoxyReturn}
